<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Vehicle_registration_plates_of_the_Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Vehicle registration plates of the Republic of Macedonia">Car plates</a></th>
<td>BT</td>
</tr>
<tr class="mergedrow">
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Climate</a></th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">Cfb</a></td>
</tr>
<tr class="mergedtoprow">
<th scope="row">Website</th>
<td><span class="url"><a class="external text" href="http://www.bitola.gov.mk" rel="nofollow">www<wbr></wbr>.bitola<wbr></wbr>.gov<wbr></wbr>.mk</a></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Bitola</b> (<a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian</a>: <span lang="mk">Битола</span> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Bulgarian_and_Macedonian" title="Help:IPA for Bulgarian and Macedonian">[ˈbitɔɫa]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata"> (<a href="/wiki/File:Mk-Bitola.ogg" title="File:Mk-Bitola.ogg"><img alt="" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" height="13" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/13px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/20px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/26px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 2x" width="13"/></a> <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4e/Mk-Bitola.ogg" title="Mk-Bitola.ogg">listen</a>)</small> known also by several <a href="#Etymology">alternative names</a>) is a city in the southwestern part of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a>. It is located in the southern part of the <a href="/wiki/Pelagonia" title="Pelagonia">Pelagonia</a> valley, surrounded by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baba_Mountain,_Macedonia" title="Baba Mountain, Macedonia">Baba</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nid%C5%BEe" title="Nidže">Nidže</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kajmak%C4%8Dalan" title="Kajmakčalan">Kajmakčalan</a> mountain ranges, 14 kilometres (9 miles) north of the <a href="/wiki/Med%C5%BEitlija-N%C3%ADki" title="Medžitlija-Níki">Medžitlija-Níki</a> border crossing with <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>. The city stands at an important junction connecting the south of the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic Sea</a> region with the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a>, and is an administrative, cultural, industrial, commercial, and educational centre. It has been known since the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> period as "the city of the consuls", since many European countries had consulates in Bitola.<br/>
Bitola is one of the oldest cities on the territory of the Republic of Macedonia, having been founded as <a href="/wiki/Heraclea_Lyncestis" title="Heraclea Lyncestis">Heraclea Lyncestis</a> in the middle of the 4th century BC by <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Macedon" title="Philip II of Macedon">Philip II of Macedon</a>. The city was the last capital of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ottoman_Rumelia" title="Ottoman Rumelia">Ottoman Rumelia</a>, from 1836–1867. According to the 2002 census, Bitola is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_the_Republic_of_Macedonia_by_population" title="List of cities in the Republic of Macedonia by population">second-largest city</a> in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Statistical_Office_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Statistical_Office-2">[2]</a></sup> Bitola is also the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Bitola_Municipality" title="Bitola Municipality">Bitola Municipality</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The name <i>Bitola</i> is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Old_Church_Slavonic" title="Old Church Slavonic">Old Church Slavonic</a> word <span class="script-slavonic" style="font-family: 'Fedorovsk Unicode', 'Fedorovsk Unicode TT', 'Menaion Unicode', 'Menaion Unicode TT', 'Monomakh Unicode', 'Monomakh Unicode TT', 'Ponomar Unicode', 'Ponomar Unicode TT', BukyVede, 'Kliment Std', 'RomanCyrillic Std', 'Monomachus', 'Old Standard', 'Old Standard TT', Dilyana, Menaion, 'Menaion Medieval', Lazov, Code2000, 'DejaVu Sans', 'DejaVu Serif', Code2001, 'FreeSerif', 'TITUS Cyberbit Basic', 'Charis SIL', 'Doulos SIL', 'Chrysanthi Unicode', 'Bitstream Cyberbit', 'Bitstream CyberBase', Thryomanes, 'Lucida Grande', 'FreeSans', 'Arial Unicode MS', 'Microsoft Sans Serif', 'Lucida Sans Unicode';" title="Slavonic">ѡ҆би́тѣл҄ь</span> (<i>obitěĺь</i>, meaning "monastery, cloister") as the city was formerly noted for its monastery. When the meaning of the name was no longer understood, it lost its prefix "o-".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> The name <i>Bitola</i> is mentioned in the <a href="/wiki/Bitola_inscription" title="Bitola inscription">Bitola inscription</a>, related to the old city fortress built in 1015. Modern Slavic variants include the <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian</a> <i>Bitola</i> (Битола), the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a> <i>Bitolj</i> (Битољ) and <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a> <i>Bitolya</i> (Битоля). In <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine</a> times, the name was Hellenized to <i>Voutélion</i> (Βουτέλιον) or <i>Vitólia</i> (Βιτώλια), hence the names <i>Butella</i> used by <a href="/wiki/William_of_Tyre" title="William of Tyre">William of Tyre</a> and <i>Butili</i> by the Arab geographer <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_al-Idrisi" title="Muhammad al-Idrisi">al-Idrisi</a>. During the ruling of Radomir Gavril(1014–1015) Bitola is mentioned under the name of Buteliu. The <a href="/wiki/Aromanian_language" title="Aromanian language">Aromanian</a> name is <i>Bituli</i>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> name for the city (<i>Monastíri</i>, Μοναστήρι), also meaning "monastery", is a <a href="/wiki/Calque" title="Calque">calque</a> of the Slavic name. The <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a> name <i>Manastır</i> (<a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkish_language" title="Ottoman Turkish language">Ottoman Turkish</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ota-Arab">مناستر</span>‎) is derived from the Greek name, as is the <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a> name (<i>Manastir</i>).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Bitola is located in the southwestern part of Macedonia. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dragor_River" title="Dragor River">Dragor River</a> flows through the city. Bitola lies at an elevation of 615 meters above sea level, at the foot of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baba_Mountain,_Macedonia" title="Baba Mountain, Macedonia">Baba Mountain</a>. Its magnificent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pelister" title="Pelister">Pelister</a> mountain (2601 m) is a national park with exquisite flora and fauna, among which is the rarest species of pine, known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macedonian_pine" title="Macedonian pine">Macedonian pine</a> or <a href="/wiki/Pinus_peuce" title="Pinus peuce">pinus peuce</a>, as well as a well-known ski resort.</p>
<p>Covering an area of 1,798 km<sup>2</sup> (694 sq mi). and with a population of 122,173 (1991), Bitola is an important industrial, agricultural, commercial, educational, and cultural center. It represents an important junction that connects the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic Sea</a> to the south with the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:958px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BitolaPanorama.jpg" title="Panorama of Bitola from Krkardaš."><img alt="" data-file-height="1330" data-file-width="5229" height="242" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/BitolaPanorama.jpg/950px-BitolaPanorama.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/BitolaPanorama.jpg/1425px-BitolaPanorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/BitolaPanorama.jpg/1900px-BitolaPanorama.jpg 2x" width="950"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BitolaPanorama.jpg" title="File:BitolaPanorama.jpg"></a></div>
Panorama of Bitola from Krkardaš.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Bitola has a mild continental climate typical of the Pelagonija region, experiencing warm and dry summers, and cold and snowy winters. The Koppen classification for this climate is Cfb.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Catolic_church_bitola.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="2048" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Catolic_church_bitola.jpg/220px-Catolic_church_bitola.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Catolic_church_bitola.jpg/330px-Catolic_church_bitola.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Catolic_church_bitola.jpg/440px-Catolic_church_bitola.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Catolic_church_bitola.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Catholic Church "Holy Heart of Jesus", on the main street of Bitola.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bitola is very rich in monuments from the prehistoric period. Two important ones are <a href="/wiki/Velu%C5%A1ka_Tumba" title="Veluška Tumba">Veluška Tumba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bara_Tumba" title="Bara Tumba">Bara Tumba</a> near the village of Porodin. From the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Copper_Age" title="Copper Age">Copper Age</a> there are the settlements of Tumba near the village of Crnobuki, Šuplevec near the village of Suvodol, and Visok Rid near the village of Bukri. The <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> is represented by the settlements of Tumba near the village of Kanino and the settlement with the same name near the village of Karamani.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_and_early_Byzantine_periods">Ancient and early Byzantine periods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Ancient and early Byzantine periods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The area of the town is located in ancient <a href="/wiki/Lynkestis" title="Lynkestis">Lynkestis</a>, a region of <a href="/wiki/Upper_Macedonia" title="Upper Macedonia">Upper Macedonia</a>, which was ruled by semi-independent chieftains till the later <a href="/wiki/Argead_dynasty" title="Argead dynasty">Argead</a> rulers of <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(ancient_kingdom)" title="Macedonia (ancient kingdom)">Macedon</a>. The tribes of Lynkestis were known as <i>Lynkestai</i>. They were a <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greek</a> tribe and belonged to the <a href="/wiki/Molossians" title="Molossians">Molossian</a> group of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Epirotes" title="Epirotes">Epirotes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> There are important metal artifacts from the ancient period at the necropolis of Crkvishte near the village of Beranci. A golden earring dating from the 4th century BC is depicted on the <a href="/wiki/Obverse_and_reverse" title="Obverse and reverse">obverse</a> of the Macedonian 10 <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_denar" title="Macedonian denar">denar</a> banknote, issued in 1996.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Heraclea_Lyncestis" title="Heraclea Lyncestis">Heraclea Lyncestis</a> (<a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">Ηράκλεια Λυγκηστίς</span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> - <i>City of Hercules upon the Land of the Lynx</i>) was an important settlement from the <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic_period" title="Hellenistic period">Hellenistic period</a> till the early <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>. It was founded by <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Macedon" title="Philip II of Macedon">Philip II of Macedon</a> by the middle of the 4th century BC, and named after the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Greek</a> hero <a href="/wiki/Heracles" title="Heracles">Heracles</a>. With its strategic location, it became a prosperous city. The <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a> conquered this part of Macedon in 148 BC and destroyed the political power of the city. However, its prosperity continued mainly due to the Roman <a href="/wiki/Via_Egnatia" title="Via Egnatia">Via Egnatia</a> road which passed near the city. Several monuments from the Roman times remain in Heraclea, including a <a href="/wiki/Portico" title="Portico">portico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thermae" title="Thermae">thermae</a> (baths), an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amphitheater" title="Amphitheater">amphitheater</a> and a number of <a href="/wiki/Basilica" title="Basilica">basilicas</a>. The theatre was once capable of housing an audience of around 3,000 people.</p>
<p>In the early <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine</a> period (4th to 6th centuries AD) Heraclea was an important episcopal centre. Some of its bishops were mentioned in the acts of the Church Councils, including Bishop Evagrius of Heraclea in the Acts of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archbishopric_of_Sardica#Council_of_Sardica" title="Archbishopric of Sardica">Sardica Council</a> of 343 AD. A small and a great (Large) basilica, the bishop's residence, and a funeral basilica near the necropolis are some of the remains of this period. Three <a href="/wiki/Nave" title="Nave">naves</a> in the Great Basilica are covered with <a href="/wiki/Mosaic" title="Mosaic">mosaics</a> of very rich floral and figurative <a href="/wiki/Iconography" title="Iconography">iconography</a>; these well preserved mosaics are often regarded as fine examples of the early <a href="/wiki/Christian_art" title="Christian art">Christian art</a> period. During the 4th and 6th centuries, the names of other bishops from Heraclea were recorded. The city was sacked by <a href="/wiki/Ostrogoths" title="Ostrogoths">Ostrogothic</a> forces, commanded by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theodoric_the_Great" title="Theodoric the Great">Theodoric the Great</a> in 472 and, despite a large gift to him from the city's bishop, it was sacked again in 479. It was restored in the late 5th and early 6th centuries. In the late 6th century the city suffered successive attacks by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slavic_peoples" title="Slavic peoples">Slavic</a> tribes and was gradually abandoned.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 6th and 7th centuries, the region around Bitola experienced a demographic shift as more and more Slavic tribes settled in the area. In place of the deserted theater, several houses were built during that time. The Slavs also built a fortress around their settlement. Bitola became a part of the <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">First Bulgarian Empire</a> from late in the 8th to early 11th centuries. The spread of Christianity was assisted by St. <a href="/wiki/Clement_of_Ohrid" title="Clement of Ohrid">Clement of Ohrid</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naum_of_Preslav" title="Naum of Preslav">Naum of Preslav</a> in the 9th and early 10th centuries. Many monasteries and churches were built in the city.</p>
<p>In the 10th century, Bitola was under the rule of the Bulgarian Tsar Samuil. He built a castle in the town, later used by his successor <a href="/wiki/Gavril_Radomir_of_Bulgaria" title="Gavril Radomir of Bulgaria">Gavril Radomir of Bulgaria</a>. The town is mentioned in several medieval sources. <a href="/wiki/John_Skylitzes" title="John Skylitzes">John Skylitzes</a>'s 11th-century chronicle mentions that Emperor <a href="/wiki/Basil_II" title="Basil II">Basil II</a> burned Gavril's castles in Bitola, when passing through and ravaging Pelagonia. The second <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chrysobull" title="Chrysobull">chrysobull</a> (1019) of Basil II mentioned that the Bishop of Bitola depended on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthodox_Archbishopric_of_Ohrid_(ancient)" title="Orthodox Archbishopric of Ohrid (ancient)">Archbishopric of Ohrid</a>. During the reign of Samuil, the city was an important centre in the Bulgarian state and the seat of the Bitola Bishopric. In many medieval sources, especially Western, the name <i>Pelagonia</i> was synonymous with the Bitola Bishopric, and in some of them Bitola was known under the name of Heraclea due to the church tradition that turned the Heraclea Bishopric into the Pelagonian Metropolitan's Diocese. In 1015, Tsar Gavril Radomir was killed by his cousin <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Vladislav_of_Bulgaria" title="Ivan Vladislav of Bulgaria">Ivan Vladislav</a>, who declared himself tsar and rebuilt the city fortress. To celebrate the occasion, a <a href="/wiki/Bitola_inscription" title="Bitola inscription">stone inscription</a> written in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cyrillic" title="Cyrillic">Cyrillic</a> alphabet was set in the fortress; in it the Slavic name of the city is mentioned: Bitol.</p>
<p>Following battles with the Tsar Ivan Vladislav, Byzantine emperor <a href="/wiki/Basil_II" title="Basil II">Basil II</a> recaptured Monastiri in 1015. The town is mentioned as an episcopal centre in 1019 in a record by Basil II. Two important uprisings against Byzantine rule took place in the Bitola area in 1040 and 1072. After the Bulgarian state was restored in the late 12th century, Bitola was incorporated under the rule of Tsar <a href="/wiki/Kaloyan_of_Bulgaria" title="Kaloyan of Bulgaria">Kaloyan of Bulgaria</a>. It was conquered again by Byzantium at the end of the 13th century, but it became part of <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> in the first half of the 14th century, after the conquests of <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Du%C5%A1an" title="Stefan Dušan">Stefan Dušan</a>.</p>
<p>As a military, political and cultural center, Bitola played a very important role in the life of the medieval society in the region, prior to the Ottoman conquest in the mid-14th century. On the eve of the Ottoman conquest, Bitola (Monastir in Ottoman Turkish) experienced great growth with its well-established trading links all over the Balkan Peninsula, especially with big economic centers like <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thessalonica" title="Thessalonica">Thessalonica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dubrovnik" title="Dubrovnik">Ragusa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Veliko_Tarnovo" title="Veliko Tarnovo">Tarnovo</a>. Caravans of various goods moved to and from Bitola.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ottoman_rule">Ottoman rule</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Ottoman rule">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Manastir_Vilayet" title="Manastir Vilayet">Manastir Vilayet</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bitola_old.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="359" data-file-width="630" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Bitola_old.jpg/220px-Bitola_old.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Bitola_old.jpg/330px-Bitola_old.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Bitola_old.jpg/440px-Bitola_old.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bitola_old.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bitola in the 19th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Greek_School_Gymnasium_of_Monastir_Bitola.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="587" data-file-width="800" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Greek_School_Gymnasium_of_Monastir_Bitola.JPG/220px-Greek_School_Gymnasium_of_Monastir_Bitola.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Greek_School_Gymnasium_of_Monastir_Bitola.JPG/330px-Greek_School_Gymnasium_of_Monastir_Bitola.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Greek_School_Gymnasium_of_Monastir_Bitola.JPG/440px-Greek_School_Gymnasium_of_Monastir_Bitola.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Greek_School_Gymnasium_of_Monastir_Bitola.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Greek school in Bitola, late 19th to early 20th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From 1382 to 1912, Manastır (now Bitola) was part of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>. Fierce battles took place near the city during the arrival of Ottoman forces. Ottoman rule was completely established after the death of <a href="/wiki/Prince_Marko" title="Prince Marko">Prince Marko</a> in 1395 when Ottoman Empire established the <a href="/wiki/Sanjak_of_Ohrid" title="Sanjak of Ohrid">Sanjak of Ohrid</a> as a part of the <a href="/wiki/Rumelia_Eyalet" title="Rumelia Eyalet">Rumelia Eyalet</a> and one of earliest established sanjaks in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Before it became part of the Ottoman Empire in 1395 its initial territory belonged to the realm of <a href="/wiki/Prince_Marko" title="Prince Marko">Prince Marko</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Initially its <a href="/wiki/County_town" title="County town">county town</a> was Bitola and later it was <a href="/wiki/Ohrid" title="Ohrid">Ohrid</a>, so it was initially sometimes referred to as Sanjak of Monastir or Sanjak of Bitola.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>For several centuries, Turks were a majority in this city, while the villages were populated mostly with Slavs. <a href="/wiki/Evliya_%C3%87elebi" title="Evliya Çelebi">Evliya Çelebi</a> says in his <i><a href="/wiki/Seyahatname" title="Seyahatname">Book of Travels</a></i> that the city had 70 mosques, several coffee-tea rooms, a <a href="/wiki/Bazaar" title="Bazaar">bazaar</a> (market) with iron gates and 900 shops. Manastır became a <a href="/wiki/Sanjak" title="Sanjak">sanjak</a> centre in the <a href="/wiki/Rumelia_Eyalet" title="Rumelia Eyalet">Rumelia Eyalet</a> (Ottoman province).</p>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_wars_in_Europe" title="Ottoman wars in Europe">Austro-Ottoman wars</a>, the trade development and the overall thriving of the city was stifled. But in the late 19th century, it again it became the second-biggest city in the wider southern Balkan region after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salonica" title="Salonica">Salonica</a>. The city is also known as "city of consuls", because 12 diplomatic consuls resided here from 1878 to 1913.</p>
<p>In 1874, Manastır became the center of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monastir_Vilayet" title="Monastir Vilayet">Monastir Vilayet</a> which included the sanjaks of <a href="/wiki/Sanjak_of_Dibra" title="Sanjak of Dibra">Debra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Servia,_Greece" title="Servia, Greece">Serfidze</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sanjak_of_Elbasan" title="Sanjak of Elbasan">Elbasan</a>, Manastır (Bitola), <a href="/wiki/Kor%C3%A7%C3%AB" title="Korçë">Görice</a> and towns of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kicevo" title="Kicevo">Kırcaova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prilep" title="Prilep">Pirlepe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florina" title="Florina">Florina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kastoria" title="Kastoria">Kesriye</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grevena" title="Grevena">Grevena</a>.</p>
<p>Traditionally a strong trading center, Bitola is also known as "the city of the consuls". At one time during the Ottoman rule, Bitola had consulates from twelve countries. During the same period, there were a number of prestigious schools in the city, including a military academy that, among others, was attended by the famous Turkish reformer <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk" title="Mustafa Kemal Atatürk">Mustafa Kemal Atatürk</a>. Bitola was also the headquarters of many cultural organizations that were established at that time.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bitola_05.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Bitola_05.JPG/220px-Bitola_05.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Bitola_05.JPG/330px-Bitola_05.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Bitola_05.JPG/440px-Bitola_05.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bitola_05.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Typical neoclassical architecture from the 19th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are opposing ethnographic data from that period, but it appears that no specific ethnic or religious group could claim an absolute majority of the population. According to the <a class="external text" href="http://www.univ.trieste.it/~storia/corsi/Dogo/tabelle/popolaz-ottomana1911.jpg" rel="nofollow">1911 Ottoman census</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a> were the largest Christian population in the vilayet, with 740,000 Greeks, 517,000 Bulgarians and 1,061,000 Muslims in the vilayets of Selanik (Thessaloniki) and Manastır. However, it should be noted that the basis of the Ottoman censuses was the millet system. People were assigned an ethnicity according to their religion. So all Sunni Muslims were categorised as Turks, although many of them were <a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">Albanians</a>, and all members of the Greek Orthodox church as Greeks, although their numbers included a vast majority of <a href="/wiki/Aromanians" title="Aromanians">Aromanians</a>, South Albanians,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> and some Macedonian Slavs. The rest were divided between Bulgarian and Serb Orthodox churches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ortayli_2006_89-8_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ortayli_2006_89-8-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Komisioni_i_Alfabetit_Monastir_1908.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="551" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Komisioni_i_Alfabetit_Monastir_1908.jpg/220px-Komisioni_i_Alfabetit_Monastir_1908.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Komisioni_i_Alfabetit_Monastir_1908.jpg/330px-Komisioni_i_Alfabetit_Monastir_1908.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Komisioni_i_Alfabetit_Monastir_1908.jpg/440px-Komisioni_i_Alfabetit_Monastir_1908.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Komisioni_i_Alfabetit_Monastir_1908.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Manastir" title="Congress of Manastir">Congress of Manastir</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bitola’s population itself was very various. It numbered some 50,000 at the end of the 19th century. There were around 7,000 Aromanians most of whom fully embraced the Hellenist ideas, although many of them joined the Romanian idea. Bitola also had significant Muslim population - 11,000 (Turks, Roma, and Albanians) as well Jewish commununity - 5,200. The Slavic-speakers were divided between the Bulgarian Exarchate - 8,000, and the Greek Patriarchate - 6,300.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1894, Manastır was connected with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salonika" title="Salonika">Selanik</a> by train. The first motion picture made in the Balkans was recorded by the <a href="/wiki/Aromanians" title="Aromanians">Aromanian</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manakis_brothers" title="Manakis brothers">Manakis brothers</a> in Manastır in 1903. In their honour, the annual Manaki Brothers International Film Camera Festival is held in modern Bitola.</p>
<p>In November 1905, the <a href="/wiki/Secret_Committee_for_the_Liberation_of_Albania" title="Secret Committee for the Liberation of Albania">Secret Committee for the Liberation of Albania</a>, a secret organization to fight for the liberation of <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> from the Ottoman Empire, was founded by <a href="/wiki/Bajo_Topulli" title="Bajo Topulli">Bajo Topulli</a> and other Albanian nationalists and intellectuals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elsie2010_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Elsie2010-18">[18]</a></sup> Three years later, the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Manastir" title="Congress of Manastir">Congress of Manastir</a> of 1908 which defined the modern <a href="/wiki/Albanian_alphabet" title="Albanian alphabet">Albanian alphabet</a> was held in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campbell2000_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Campbell2000-19">[19]</a></sup> The congress was held at the house of <a href="/wiki/Fehim_Zavalani" title="Fehim Zavalani">Fehim Zavalani</a> and led by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mit%27hat_Frash%C3%ABri" title="Mit'hat Frashëri">Mit'hat Frashëri</a>, chairman of the congress. The participants in the Congress were prominent figures of the cultural and political life from Albanian-inhabited territories in the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a>, as well as throughout the <a href="/wiki/Albanian_diaspora" title="Albanian diaspora">Albanian diaspora</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ilinden_Uprising">Ilinden Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Ilinden Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bitola.1914.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="735" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Bitola.1914.jpg/220px-Bitola.1914.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Bitola.1914.jpg/330px-Bitola.1914.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Bitola.1914.jpg/440px-Bitola.1914.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bitola.1914.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Street in Bitola in 1914</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Bitola region was a stronghold of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ilinden-Preobrazhenie_Uprising" title="Ilinden-Preobrazhenie Uprising">Ilinden Uprising</a>. The uprising was started as decided in 1903 in Thessaloniki by the <a href="/wiki/Internal_Macedonian_Revolutionary_Organization" title="Internal Macedonian Revolutionary Organization">Internal Macedonian Revolutionary Organization</a> (IMRO). The uprising in the Bitola region was planned in <a href="/wiki/Smilevo" title="Smilevo">Smilevo</a> village in May 1903. The battles were fought in the villages of Bistrica, Rakovo, Buf, Skocivir, Paralovo, Brod, Novaci, Smilevo, Gjavato, Capari and others. Smilevo was defended by 600 rebels led by <a href="/wiki/Dame_Gruev" title="Dame Gruev">Dame Gruev</a> and <a href="/wiki/Georgi_Sugarev" title="Georgi Sugarev">Georgi Sugarev</a>, but when they were defeated, villages were burned.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Balkan_Wars">Balkan Wars</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Balkan Wars">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1912, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> fought the Ottomans in the <a href="/wiki/First_Balkan_War" title="First Balkan War">First Balkan War</a>. After victory <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sarantaporo" title="Battle of Sarantaporo">at Sarantaporo</a>, Greek troops advanced towards Monastir but were defeated by the Ottomans <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sorovich" title="Battle of Sorovich">at Sorovich</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Monastir" title="Battle of Monastir">Battle of Monastir</a> (16–19 November 1912) led to Serbian occupation. According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Bucharest,_1913" title="Treaty of Bucharest, 1913">Treaty of Bucharest, 1913</a>, the region of Macedonia was divided into three parts between Greece, Serbia and Bulgaria, with Monastir ceded to Serbia, given the name <i>Bitola</i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_I">World War I</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: World War I">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:72px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vivat-bander_-_1915-12-04_-_Monastir_by_O._R._Bossert.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="9909" data-file-width="2047" height="339" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Vivat-bander_-_1915-12-04_-_Monastir_by_O._R._Bossert.jpg/70px-Vivat-bander_-_1915-12-04_-_Monastir_by_O._R._Bossert.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Vivat-bander_-_1915-12-04_-_Monastir_by_O._R._Bossert.jpg/105px-Vivat-bander_-_1915-12-04_-_Monastir_by_O._R._Bossert.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Vivat-bander_-_1915-12-04_-_Monastir_by_O._R._Bossert.jpg/140px-Vivat-bander_-_1915-12-04_-_Monastir_by_O._R._Bossert.jpg 2x" width="70"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vivat-bander_-_1915-12-04_-_Monastir_by_O._R._Bossert.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
German <a href="/wiki/Vivat_ribbons" title="Vivat ribbons">Vivat ribbon</a> commemorating the Bulgarian occupation (1915).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> Bitola was on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salonica_Front" title="Salonica Front">Salonica Front</a>. Bulgaria, a <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Power</a>, took the city on 21 November 1915, while the Allied forces <a href="/wiki/Monastir_Offensive" title="Monastir Offensive">recaptured it in 1916</a>. Bitola was divided into French, Russian, Italian and Serbian sections, under the command of French general <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Sarrail" title="Maurice Sarrail">Maurice Sarrail</a>. Until Bulgaria's surrender in late autumn 1918, Bitola remained a front line city and was almost daily bombarded by air and battery and suffered almost total destruction.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inter-war_period">Inter-war period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Inter-war period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>AT the end of World War I Bitola was restored to the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia" title="Kingdom of Serbia">Kingdom of Serbia</a>, and, consequently, became part in 1918 of the Kingdom of Serbs, Croats and Slovenes, renamed Yugoslavia in 1929. Bitola became one of the major cities of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vardarska_banovina" title="Vardarska banovina">Vardarska banovina</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> (1941–45), the Germans (on 9 April 1941) and later Bulgarians (on 18 April 1941) took control of the city. But in September 1944, Bulgaria switched sides in the war and withdrew from Yugoslavia, and Bitola was freed by the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Partisans" title="Yugoslav Partisans">Yugoslav Partisans</a>. On 4 November, the 7th Macedonian Liberation Brigade entered Bitola victoriously. A <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Monastir" title="History of the Jews in Monastir">historical Jewish community</a>, of Sephardic origin, lived in the city until World War II, when mostly were killed or migrated to the United States and Chile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> After the end of the war, a Macedonian state was established for the first time in modern history, within Yugoslavia. This had cost about 25,000 human lives. In 1945, the first Gymnasium (named "<a href="/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito" title="Josip Broz Tito">Josip Broz Tito</a>") to use the Macedonian language, was opened in Bitola.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_sights">Main sights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Main sights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The city has many historical building dating from many historical periods. The most notable ones are from the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman age</a>, but there are some from the more recent past.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id=".C5.A0irok_Sokak">Širok Sokak</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Širok Sokak">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0irok_Sokak" title="Širok Sokak">Širok Sokak</a></div>
<p>Širok Sokak (<a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian</a>: <span lang="mk">Широк Сокак</span>, meaning "Wide Alley") is a long <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pedestrian_street" title="Pedestrian street">pedestrian street</a> that runs from <a href="/wiki/Magnolia_Square" title="Magnolia Square">Magnolia Square</a> to the City Park.</p>

</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Clock_Tower">Clock Tower</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Clock Tower">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%90%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D0%91%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0,_%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BA%D1%83%D1%9C%D0%B0.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/%D0%90%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D0%91%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0%2C_%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BA%D1%83%D1%9C%D0%B0.jpg/220px-%D0%90%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D0%91%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0%2C_%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BA%D1%83%D1%9C%D0%B0.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/%D0%90%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D0%91%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0%2C_%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BA%D1%83%D1%9C%D0%B0.jpg/330px-%D0%90%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D0%91%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0%2C_%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BA%D1%83%D1%9C%D0%B0.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/%D0%90%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D0%91%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0%2C_%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BA%D1%83%D1%9C%D0%B0.jpg/440px-%D0%90%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D0%91%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0%2C_%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%B0_%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%BA%D1%83%D1%9C%D0%B0.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

<a href="/wiki/Turkish_bath" title="Turkish bath">Turkish bath</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:St._Demetrius_Church_in_Bitola_8.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4272" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/St._Demetrius_Church_in_Bitola_8.JPG/220px-St._Demetrius_Church_in_Bitola_8.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/St._Demetrius_Church_in_Bitola_8.JPG/330px-St._Demetrius_Church_in_Bitola_8.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/St._Demetrius_Church_in_Bitola_8.JPG/440px-St._Demetrius_Church_in_Bitola_8.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:St._Demetrius_Church_in_Bitola_8.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
St. Demetrius Church in Bitola</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>It is unknown when Bitola's <a href="/wiki/Clock_tower" title="Clock tower">clock tower</a> was built. Written sources from the 16th century mention a clock tower, but it is not clear if it is the same one. Some believe it was built at the same time as St. Dimitrija Church, in 1830. Legend says that the Ottoman authorities collected around 60,000 eggs from nearby villages and mixed them in the <a href="/wiki/Mortar_(masonry)" title="Mortar (masonry)">mortar</a> to make the walls stronger.</p>
<p>The tower has a rectangular base and is about 30 meters high. Near the top is a rectangular terrace with an iron fence. On each side of the fence is an iron console construction which holds the lamps for lighting the clock. The clock is on the highest of three levels. The original clock was replaced during World War II with a working one, given by the Nazis because the city had maintained German graves from World War I. The massive tower is composed of walls, massive spiral stairs, wooden mezzanine constructions, <a href="/wiki/Pendentive" title="Pendentive">pendentives</a> and the dome. During the construction of the tower, the façade was simultaneously decorated with simple stone plastic.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Church_of_Saint_Demetrius">Church of Saint Demetrius</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Church of Saint Demetrius">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Church of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Demetrius" title="Saint Demetrius">Saint Demetrius</a> was built in 1830 with voluntary contributions of local merchants and craftsmen. It is plain on the outside, as all churches in the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> had to be, but of rare beauty inside, lavishly decorated with <a href="/wiki/Chandelier" title="Chandelier">chandeliers</a>, a carved bishop throne and an engraved <a href="/wiki/Iconostasis" title="Iconostasis">iconostasis</a>. According to some theories, the iconostasis is a work of the <a href="/wiki/Mijaks" title="Mijaks">Mijak</a> engravers. Its most impressive feature is the arc above the imperial quarters with modeled figures of <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus</a> and the apostles.</p>
<p>Other engraved wood items include the bishop's throne made in the spirit of Mijak engravers, several <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Icon_frames&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Icon frames (page does not exist)">icon frames</a> and five more-recent pillars shaped like thrones. The frescoes originate from two periods: the end of the 19th century, and the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> to the present. The icons and frescoes were created thanks to voluntary contributions of local businessmen and citizens. The authors of many of the icons had a vast knowledge of iconography schemes of the <a href="/wiki/New_Testament" title="New Testament">New Testament</a>. The icons show a great sense of color, dominated by red, green and ochra shades. The abundance of golden ornaments is noticeable and points to the presence of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late-Byzantine" title="Late-Byzantine">late-Byzantine</a> artwork and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baroque_style" title="Baroque style">baroque style</a>. The icon of Saint Demetrius is signed with the initials "D. A. Z.", showing that it was made by iconographer Dimitar Andonov the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Zograph&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Zograph (page does not exist)">zograph</a> in 1889. There are many other items, including the <a href="/wiki/Chalice" title="Chalice">chalices</a> made by local masters, a darohranilka of Russian origin, and several paintings of scenes from the New Testament, brought from Jerusalem by pilgrims.</p>
<p>The opening scenes of the film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Peacemaker_(1997_film)" title="The Peacemaker (1997 film)">The Peacemaker</a></i> were shot in the "St. Dimitrija" church in Bitola, as well as some <i><a href="/wiki/Welcome_to_Sarajevo" title="Welcome to Sarajevo">Welcome to Sarajevo</a></i> scenes.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Heraclea_Lyncestis">Heraclea Lyncestis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Heraclea Lyncestis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Heraclea_Lyncestis" title="Heraclea Lyncestis">Heraclea Lyncestis</a> (<a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian</a>: <span lang="mk">Хераклеа Линкестис</span>) was an important ancient settlement from the <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic_period" title="Hellenistic period">Hellenistic period</a> till the early Middle Ages. It was founded by <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Macedon" title="Philip II of Macedon">Philip II of Macedon</a> by the middle of the 4th century BC. Today, its ruins fall in the southern part of Bitola, 2 km (1 mi) from the city center.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_covered_bazaar">The covered bazaar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: The covered bazaar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bitola.1914_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="504" data-file-width="812" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Bitola.1914_01.jpg/250px-Bitola.1914_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Bitola.1914_01.jpg/375px-Bitola.1914_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Bitola.1914_01.jpg/500px-Bitola.1914_01.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bitola.1914_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Monastir bazaar in 1914</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Situated near the city centre, the covered <a href="/wiki/Bazaar" title="Bazaar">bazaar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian</a>: <span lang="mk">Bezisten, Безистен</span>) is one of the most impressive and oldest buildings in Bitola from the Turkish period. With its numerous cupolas that look like a fortress, with its tree-branch-like inner streets and four big metal doors it is one of the biggest covered markets in the region.</p>
<p>It was built in the 15th century by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Kara_Daut_Pasha_Uzuncarsili&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Kara Daut Pasha Uzuncarsili (page does not exist)">Kara Daut Pasha Uzuncarsili</a>, then <a href="/wiki/Rumelia_Eyalet" title="Rumelia Eyalet">Rumelia</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Beylerbey" title="Beylerbey">Beylerbey</a>. Although the object looks secure, many times during its existence has been robbed and set on fire, but it managed to survive. The Bezisten, from the 15th to the 19th centuries, was rebuilt, and many stores, often changing over time, were located there. Most of them were selling textile and other luxurious fabrics. At the same time the Bezisten was a treasury, where in specially made small rooms the money from the whole Rumelian Vilaet was kept, before it was transferred into the royal treasury. In the 19th century the Bezisten held a total of 84 shops. Today most of them are contemporary and they sell different types of products, but no matter what the internal transformations, the outer appearance has stayed unchanged.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gazi_Hajdar_Kadi_Mosque">Gazi Hajdar Kadi Mosque</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Gazi Hajdar Kadi Mosque">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Gazi_Hajdar_Kadi_Mosque" title="Gazi Hajdar Kadi Mosque">Gazi Hajdar Kadi Mosque</a> is one of the most attractive monuments of Islamic architecture in Bitola. It was built in the early 1560s, as the project of the famous architect <a href="/wiki/Mimar_Sinan" title="Mimar Sinan">Mimar Sinan</a>, ordered by the Bitola kadija Ajdar-kadi. Over time, it was abandoned and heavily damaged, and at one point used as a stare,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> but recent restoration and conservation has restored to some extent its original appearance.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jeni_Mosque">Jeni Mosque</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Jeni Mosque">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2011_Bitola,_Meczet_Jeni_01.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4168" data-file-width="2778" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/2011_Bitola%2C_Meczet_Jeni_01.JPG/170px-2011_Bitola%2C_Meczet_Jeni_01.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/2011_Bitola%2C_Meczet_Jeni_01.JPG/255px-2011_Bitola%2C_Meczet_Jeni_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/2011_Bitola%2C_Meczet_Jeni_01.JPG/340px-2011_Bitola%2C_Meczet_Jeni_01.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2011_Bitola,_Meczet_Jeni_01.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jeni_Mosque" title="Jeni Mosque">Jeni Mosque</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jeni_Mosque" title="Jeni Mosque">Jeni Mosque</a> is located in the center of the city. It has a square base, topped with a dome. Near the mosque is a minaret, 40 m high. Today, the mosque's rooms house permanent and temporary art exhibitions. Recent archaeological excavations have revealed that it has been built upon an old church.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ishak_.C3.87elebi_Mosque">Ishak Çelebi Mosque</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Ishak Çelebi Mosque">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ishak_%C3%87elebi_Mosque" title="Ishak Çelebi Mosque">Ishak Çelebi Mosque</a> is the inheritance of the kadi <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ishak_%C3%87elebi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ishak Çelebi (page does not exist)">Ishak Çelebi</a>. In its spacious yard are several tombs, attractive because of the soft, molded shapes of the sarcophagi.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kod.C5.BEa_Kadi_Mosque">Kodža Kadi Mosque</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Kodža Kadi Mosque">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_old_bazaar">The old bazaar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: The old bazaar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The old <a href="/wiki/Bazaar" title="Bazaar">bazaar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian</a>: <i>Стара Чаршија</i>) is mentioned in a description of the city from the 16th and the 17th centuries. The present <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bezisten" title="Bezisten">bezisten</a> does not differ much in appearance from the original one. The bezisten had eighty-six shops and four large iron gates. The shops used to sell textiles, and today sell food products.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Deboj_Bath">Deboj Bath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Deboj Bath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Deboj Bath is a <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Turkish</a> bath (<a href="/wiki/Turkish_bath" title="Turkish bath">hamam</a>). It is not known when exactly it was constructed. At one point, it was heavily damaged, but after repairs it regained its original appearance: a beautiful façade, two large domes and several minor ones.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Bitola_today">Bitola today</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Bitola today">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bitola_Zoo_Lions_2.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1224" data-file-width="1632" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Bitola_Zoo_Lions_2.JPG/220px-Bitola_Zoo_Lions_2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Bitola_Zoo_Lions_2.JPG/330px-Bitola_Zoo_Lions_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Bitola_Zoo_Lions_2.JPG/440px-Bitola_Zoo_Lions_2.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bitola_Zoo_Lions_2.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Lion" title="Lion">lions</a> in their cage at Bitola zoo</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bitola is the economic and industrial center of southwestern Macedonia. Many of the largest companies in the country are based in the city. The Pelagonia agricultural <a href="/wiki/Combine_(enterprise)" title="Combine (enterprise)">combine</a> is the largest producer of food in the country. The Streževo water system is the largest in the Republic of Macedonia and has the best technological facilities. The three thermoelectric power stations of REK Bitola produce nearly 80% of electricity in the state. The Frinko refrigerate factory was a leading electrical and metal company. Bitola also has significant capacity in the textile and food industries.</p>
<p>Bitola is also home to twelve <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Consulate" title="Consulate">consulates</a>, which gives the city the nickname "the city of consuls."</p>

<p>Also, Albania<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> and Italy<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> expressed interest in opening a consulate in Bitola.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are three Bitola Television Stations: Tera, Orbis and Mega, two regional radio stations: the private Radio 105, Aktuel Bombarder and Radio Delfin as well as a local weekly newspaper — Bitolski Vesnik.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="City_Council">City Council</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: City Council">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Composition_of_Bitola_Council.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="185" data-file-width="360" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Composition_of_Bitola_Council.svg/220px-Composition_of_Bitola_Council.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Composition_of_Bitola_Council.svg/330px-Composition_of_Bitola_Council.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Composition_of_Bitola_Council.svg/440px-Composition_of_Bitola_Council.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Composition_of_Bitola_Council.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The composition of the council:<br/>
<span style="background-color:#8F1F29; color:; border:1px solid #000000; text-align:center;">    </span> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internal_Macedonian_Revolutionary_Organization_%E2%80%93_Democratic_Party_for_Macedonian_National_Unity" title="Internal Macedonian Revolutionary Organization – Democratic Party for Macedonian National Unity">Internal Macedonian Revolutionary Organization – Democratic Party for Macedonian National Unity</a> (17)<br/>
<span style="background-color:#4141EB; color:; border:1px solid #000000; text-align:center;">    </span> <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Union_of_Macedonia" title="Social Democratic Union of Macedonia">Social Democratic Union of Macedonia</a> (9)<br/>
<span style="background-color:#49EB41; color:; border:1px solid #000000; text-align:center;">    </span> <a href="/wiki/Internal_Macedonian_Revolutionary_Organization_%E2%80%93_People%27s_Party" title="Internal Macedonian Revolutionary Organization – People's Party">Internal Macedonian Revolutionary Organization – People's Party</a> (2)<br/>
<span style="background-color:#E541EB; color:; border:1px solid #000000; text-align:center;">    </span> <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democratic_Party_(Republic_of_Macedonia)" title="Liberal Democratic Party (Republic of Macedonia)">Liberal Democratic Party of Macedonia</a> (2)<br/>
<span style="background-color:#EBA941; color:; border:1px solid #000000; text-align:center;">    </span> <a href="/wiki/Party_of_United_Democrats_of_Macedonia" title="Party of United Democrats of Macedonia">Party of United Democrats of Macedonia</a> (1)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <b>Bitola Municipality Council</b> (<a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian</a>: <span lang="mk">Совет на Општина Битола</span>) is the <a href="/wiki/City_council" title="City council">governing body</a> of the city and municipality of Bitola. The city council approves and rejects projects that would have place inside the municipality given by its members and the Mayor of Bitola. The Council consists of representatives of citizens elected by direct and free <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elections" title="Elections">elections</a>. The number of members of the council is determined according to the number of residents in the community and can not be fewer than nine nor more than 33. Accordingly, the number of residents, the Council of Bitola municipality is composed of 31 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Councilor" title="Councilor">councilors</a>. Council members are elected for a term of four years.</p>
<p>Since 2013, the council consists of representatives of five political parties: <a href="/wiki/VMRO-DPMNE" title="VMRO-DPMNE">VMRO-DPMNE</a> - 17, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SDSM" title="SDSM">SDSM</a> - 9, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VMRO-NP" title="VMRO-NP">VMRO-NP</a> - 2, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PODEM" title="PODEM">PODEM</a> - 1 and <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democratic_Party_(Republic_of_Macedonia)" title="Liberal Democratic Party (Republic of Macedonia)">Liberal Democratic Party of Macedonia</a> - 2.</p>
<p>Examining matters within its competence, the Council set up <a href="/wiki/Committee" title="Committee">committees</a>. Council committees are formed as permanent and temporary.</p>
<p>Permanent committees of the Council:</p>
<ul>
<li>Finance and Budget Committee;</li>
<li>Commission for Public Utilities;</li>
<li>Committee on Urban Planning, public works and environmental protection;</li>
<li>Commission for social activities;</li>
<li>Commission for local government;</li>
<li>Commission to mark holidays, events and award certificates and awards;</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The most popular sports in Bitola are <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Team_handball" title="Team handball">handball</a>.</p>
<p>The main football team is <a href="/wiki/FK_Pelister" title="FK Pelister">FK Pelister</a> and they play at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tumbe_Kafe_Stadium" title="Tumbe Kafe Stadium">Tumbe Kafe Stadium</a> which has a capacity of 8,000. <a href="/wiki/Gjorgji_Hristov" title="Gjorgji Hristov">Gjorgji Hristov</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dragan_Kanatlarovski" title="Dragan Kanatlarovski">Dragan Kanatlarovski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toni_Micevski" title="Toni Micevski">Toni Micevski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nikol%C4%8De_Noveski" title="Nikolče Noveski">Nikolče Noveski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toni_Savevski" title="Toni Savevski">Toni Savevski</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mitko_Stojkovski" title="Mitko Stojkovski">Mitko Stojkovski</a> are some of the famous Bitola natives to start their careers with the club.</p>
<p>The main handball club and most famous sports team from Bitola is <a href="/wiki/RK_Pelister" title="RK Pelister">RK Pelister</a>. <a href="/wiki/RK_Bitola" title="RK Bitola">RK Bitola</a> is the second club from the city and both teams play their games at the <a href="/wiki/Sports_Hall_Mladost" title="Sports Hall Mladost">Sports Hall Mladost</a>.</p>
<p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macedonian_Second_League" title="Macedonian Second League">Macedonian Second League</a>, <a href="/wiki/FK_Novaci" title="FK Novaci">FK Novaci</a> are competing, which is located in the Region of Bitola.</p>
<p>All the sports teams under the name <i>Pelister</i> are supported by the fans known as <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Ckembari" title="Čkembari">Čkembari</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bitola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>Ethnic groups</dt>
</dl>
<p>According to the 1948 census Bitola had 30,761 inhabitants. 77.2% (or 23,734 inhabitants) were Macedonians, 11.5% (or 3,543 inhabitants) were Turks, 4.3% (or 1,327 inhabitants) were Albanians, 3% (or 912 inhabitants) were Serbs and 1.3% (or 402 inhabitants) were Aromanians. As of 2002, the city of Bitola has 74,550 inhabitants and the ethnic composition is the following:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.D0.BF.D0.BE.D0.BF.D0.B8.D1.81_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-.D0.BF.D0.BE.D0.BF.D0.B8.D1.81-31">[31]</a></sup></p>

srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%88%D1%82%D0%B5_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE-%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%85%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0_%D1%81%D0%B5_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BE%D1%93%D0%B0_%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%91%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0.jpg/330px-%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%88%D1%82%D0%B5_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE-%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%85%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0_%D1%81%D0%B5_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BE%D1%93%D0%B0_%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%91%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%88%D1%82%D0%B5_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE-%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%85%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0_%D1%81%D0%B5_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BE%D1%93%D0%B0_%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%91%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0.jpg/440px-%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%88%D1%82%D0%B5_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE-%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%85%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0_%D1%81%D0%B5_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BE%D1%93%D0%B0_%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%91%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%88%D1%82%D0%B5_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE-%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%85%D0%B8%D1%98%D0%B0_%D1%81%D0%B5_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BE%D1%93%D0%B0_%D0%B2%D0%BE_%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%91%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The seat of Prespa- Pelagonia diocese of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macedonian_Orthodox_Church_-_Ohrid_Archbishopric" title="Macedonian Orthodox Church - Ohrid Archbishopric">Macedonian Orthodox Church - Ohrid Archbishopric</a> in Bitola</div>
</div>
</div>
</dd>
</dl>
<p>Bitola is a bishopric city and the seat of the Diocese of Prespa- Pelagonia. In <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> the diocese was named Ohrid - Bitola. With the restoration of the autocephaly of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macedonian_Orthodox_Church_-_Ohrid_Archbishopric" title="Macedonian Orthodox Church - Ohrid Archbishopric">Macedonian Orthodox Church</a> in 1967, it got its present name Prespa- Pelagonia diocese which covers the following regions and cities: Bitola, <a href="/wiki/Resen_Municipality" title="Resen Municipality">Resen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prilep" title="Prilep">Prilep</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Krusevo" title="Krusevo">Krusevo</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Demir_Hisar_municipality" title="Demir Hisar municipality">Demir Hisar</a>.</p>
<p>The first bishop of the diocese (1958 - 1979) was Mr. Kliment. The second and current bishop and administrator of the diocese, responsible as bishop since 1981 is Mr. Petar. The Prespa- Pelagonia diocese has about 500 churches and monasteries. In the last ten years in the diocese have been built or are being built about 40 churches and 140 church buildings. The diocese has two church museums- the cathedral "St. Martyr Demetrius" in Bitola and at the Church "St. John" in Krusevo and permanent exhibition of icons and libraries in the building of the seat of the diocese. The seat building was built between 1901 and 1902 and is one of the most beautiful examples of the baroque architecture. Besides the dominant Macedonian Orthodox Church in Bitola there are other major religious groups such as the <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_the_Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Islam in the Republic of Macedonia">Islamic community</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Greek_Catholic_Church" title="Macedonian Greek Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a> and others.</p>
<p>According to the 2002 census the religious composition of the city is the following:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.D0.BF.D0.BE.D0.BF.D0.B8.D1.81_31-4"><a href="#cite_note-.D0.BF.D0.BE.D0.BF.D0.B8.D1.81-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
